     <div id="main"> 
      <div id="ctl00_PlaceHolderMain_ctl00__ControlWrapper_RichHtmlField" style="display: inline"> 
       <div class="first-readHome"> 
        <h3>Highlander Union</h3> 
        <em>The Highlander Union is a gathering place where you and your friends can meet, eat, relax and study. It features dining and retail facilities, meeting areas, lounges and event spaces. The HUB also provides offices for student government, student organizations, and student affairs. But, if you have a question or need directions to your next campus destination, ask a service associate at the Welcome Desk, located on the first floor of the main building.</em>
        <br /> 
        <h4>Meet</h4> Student organizations, campus members and off-campus groups have the selection of hosting their meeting or program in any of the HUB conference rooms or surrounding outdoor locations. 
        <a href="../EventScheduling/Pages/CommonsEventScheduling.aspx"><strong>Highlander Event Scheduling</strong></a> can assist you with a reservation to make sure you have everything you need for the event.
        <p></p> 
        <h4>Eat</h4> 
        <p> The dining restaurants at the HUB offer a range of fare, from burgers, sushi and tacos to Chinese and Italian inspired cuisine. For those on the go, the Scotty's convenience store is a quick stop to pick up a snack. If youre looking to feed a few more individuals in addition to yourself, Dining Services offers convenient catering for any event or gathering youre hosting on campus. For current hours of operation for HUB restaurants, <a href="http://dining.ucr.edu/CampusRestaurants/Pages/TheHubRestaurants.aspx"><strong>click here</strong></a>. </p> 
        <h4>Relax</h4> 
        <p> The Highlander Union is a great location to gather with friends or to take it easy during a busy day of instruction, labs and discussions. The outdoor plaza and lounges provide shady and suitable sitting areas among the Unions landscape. So whether you choose to play a game of pool in Latitude Fifty-Five or watch whats on TV in the lounge, the Highlander Union has a lot to offer to anyone who visits. </p> 
        <h4>Study</h4> 
        <p> In keeping with the educational mission of the University, the Highlander Union has multiple lounge areas throughout the building to provide comfy places to study. The Union offers the Universitys wi-fi connection in and around the building. All you need to access it is your student username and password. </p> 
        <p> If you are a scholarly graduate student, theres also the Graduate Student Lounge on the third floor of the Union, which overlooks the Plaza and has a great view of the Box Spring Mountains. </p> 
        <p> During finals week, all meeting rooms in the Union are open as study rooms, no reservation required. Each room has ample space for multiple study groups and most rooms have a dry-erase board. For those studying diligently late at night, the Union is conveniently open until midnight during finals week. </p> 
        <p> <br /> </p> 
        <h3>Construction</h3> 
        <p>It took three full years for the Highlander Union to rise from a flat patch of dirt. But you can see it all in just 20 seconds.</p> 
        <br />

            pageTracker._setDomainName("highlanderunionbuilding.ucr.edu");
            pageTracker._trackPageview();
        } catch(err) {}

            var pageTracker2 = _gat._getTracker("UA-3051875-1");
            pageTracker2._setDomainName("ucr.edu");
            pageTracker2._trackPageview();
        } catch(err) {}

     <script type="text/javascript">

var calserver = "http://ragsm.ucr.edu/agsmevents/";
var prog      = "mba";
var ishover   = false;
var autorate  = 7;
var animrate  = 'fast';

function scarousel_initCallback(carousel) {
  $('#jd_news_sidebar').hover(function() {
	ishover = true;
    carousel.startAuto(0);
    carousel.animation(0);
  }, function() {
    ishover = false;
    carousel.animation(animrate);
    carousel.startAuto(autorate);
  });

}

$(document).ready(function(){

  var path = document.location.pathname;
  var dir = path.substring(path.indexOf('/', 0)+1, path.lastIndexOf('/'));

  if (dir == "calendar") {
    $("#sidebar_events").hide();
  } else {
    $.getJSON(calserver + "ae_get_website_sidebar.php?jsoncallback=?&prog="+prog,
    function(data) {
      $("#jd_news_sidebar").html(data.sidebar);
      $('#jd_news_sidebar ul').attr('id','sidebar_carousel');
      //$('div.jd_news_scroll').jdNewsScroll();
      $('#sidebar_carousel').jcarousel({
        initCallback: scarousel_initCallback,
        vertical: true,
        scroll: 1,
        auto: autorate,
		wrap: 'last',
		animation: animrate
      });
    });
  }

});

</script>

       <!-- ouc:editor csspath="/z-omniupdate/css/style.css" cssmenu="/z-omniupdate/css/style.txt" width="460"/ -->
       <h3>iLearn connection issues and/or SafeAssign submissions issues? Please go to our FAQ page for possible solutions.</h3> 
       <p>&nbsp;</p> 
       <h3>iLearn has been upgraded to version 13.</h3> 
       <p>Computing &amp; Communications has performed over the holiday break a Blackboard application version update as well as a database upgrade to our learning management system, iLearn. This upgrade needed to be performed in order to bring iLearn to a supported version, enhance functionality, address some bugs and optimize performance of the system. iLearn is now fully available.</p> 
       <p>We have moved from Blackboard 9.1 SP 10 to SP 13. Although there were no major changes to iLearn, this version introduces a sleeker interface with some functionality improvements but still maintains the old look of buttons. In the Spring quarter, course sites will reflect the newer text view with no buttons. If the button view is preferred, customization allows an instructor to revert to the button view.</p> 
       <p><a title="New Feature Showcase" href="http://www.blackboard.com/Platforms/Learn/Products/Blackboard-Learn/Features.aspx#test-enhancements" target="_blank">New Features Showcase</a></p> 
       <p>Please join our Instructional Technology team each Wednesday during drop-in hours for Blackboard support if you would like an informational session as to new features:</p> 
       <p>o Location: Surge 170<br />o Date: Every Wednesdays during the quarter.&nbsp; (same place; same time)<br />o Time: 1:00-3:00PM</p> 
       <p>For more information, please visit this website http://cnc.ucr.edu/ilearn or contact the helpdesk@ucr.edu with any questions about the update.</p> ------------------------------------ 
       <h3>Workshop Sessions: &quot;Tools for Enhanced/Blended/Hybrid Teaching and Learning&quot;</h3> 
       <p>Faculty Technology Support invites teaching Faculty/TAs for a brief presentation/discussion session,&nbsp;&quot;Tools for Enhanced/Blended/Hybrid Teaching and Learning&quot;. These sessions will focus on the technologies generally available to the campus such as course capturing, virtual collaboration, social media tools as well as developing a supporting course site in iLearn.</p> 
       <p>Time: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Mar. 13th, at 11:00-Noon.<br />Location: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Hyperstruction Studio, Surge 170.<br />Format: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Presentation, discussion, workshop.</p> 
       <p>C&amp;C's Winter 2014 Technology workshop series is composed of general sessions followed by topic specific sessions. The general sessions are scheduled on Tuesdays, discussing overall online design elements, focusing on building an enhanced/blended/hybrid learning environment within a supporting course site in iLearn. The topic specific sessions are scheduled on Thursdays, focusing in depth on a specific topic, component, or technology used in course delivery.</p> 
       <p>We hope to see you during the Winter quarter at one or more of the following sessions:</p> 
       <p>1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Seminars:&nbsp;Designing Enhanced/Blended/Hybrid&nbsp; Courses in iLearn Mar 13th, 11:00-Noon, Surge 170</p> 
       <p>2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Workshop 1: Using Lecture Capture Mar 6th, 11:00-Noon, Surge 170</p> 
       <p>3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Workshop 2: Web Collaboration with Adobe Connect Mar, 20th 11:00-Noon, Surge 170</p> 
       <p>4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Workshop 3:&nbsp; Social Media Tools in iLearn Mar TBD 11:00-Noon, Surge 170</p> 
       <p>Light refreshments will be served. An RSVP is kindly requested to:&nbsp; ilearn@ucr.edu.</p> 
       <h3>iLearn 9.1.13 update is now available for Winter quarter 2014 for all students and faculty.</h3> 
       <p>Now available for all mobile devices and smart phones.</p> 
       <p>iLearn Mobile Learn platform takes interactive teaching and learning mobile, giving students and educators access to their courses, content and organizations on a variety of devices including iOS&reg;, Android™, BlackBerry&reg;, and webOS&reg; smartphones.</p> 
       <p><a href="http://www.blackboard.com/Platforms/Mobile/Resources/Blackboard-Mobile-Learn-Adoption-Kit.aspx" target="_blank">iLearn Mobile Adoption Kit</a></p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Best Practices for Mobile-friendly courses</li> 
        <li>Faculty guide to mobile tests</li> 
       </ul> You can link your Dropbox account to iLearn Mobile Learn on your iOS and Android device!
       <!-- /com.omniupdate.div -->

       <h6><em>Check out some of the new features in Blackboard 9.1 </em></h6> 
       <p><a onclick="return hs.expand(this, {captionId: 'caption1'})" href="/ilearn/images/grade_center_colors.jpg"><img src="/ilearn/images/grade_center_colors.jpg" alt="edit mode" width="205" height="149" /></a><br /> With new Grade Center Smart Views you can create criteria for sorting grades and add color coding based on your criteria.</p> 
       <p><a onclick="return hs.expand(this, {captionId: 'caption1'})" href="/ilearn/images/create_rubric.jpg"><img src="/ilearn/images/create_rubric.jpg" alt="create new item" width="205" height="114" /></a><br /> The new Rubric Tool allows you to create your own custom grading rubric and apply it to Assignments, Blogs and Wikis, and Essay, Short Answer and File Response test questions.</p> 
       <p><a onclick="return hs.expand(this, {captionId: 'caption1'})" href="/ilearn/images/mashups.jpg"><img src="/ilearn/images/mashups.jpg" alt="content areas" width="205" height="110" /></a><br />The new Build Content menu offers more choices for content type including YouTube videos, Flickr images and Slideshare documents.</p>

     <a name="Top of Page"> </a> 
     <h3><img class="img_L" title="Mark Hoddle" src="/images/mark_hoddle_ucr.jpg" alt="Mark Hoddle" width="150" height="182" />Mark S. Hoddle, Ph.D.<br /><span style="color: #25558c; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px; font-weight: bold;">Biological Control Specialist and Principal Investigator<br /></span><span style="color: #25558c; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px; font-weight: bold;">Phone: (951) 827-4714<br /></span><span style="color: #25558c; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px; font-weight: bold;">Fax: (951) 827-3086<br /></span><span style="color: #25558c; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px; font-weight: bold;"><a href="mailto:mark.hoddle@ucr.edu">mark.hoddle@ucr.edu</a></span></h3> 
     <p>Dr. Hoddle has headed the research in this laboratory since 1997 and is primarily involved in the identification of pest problems where biological control could be a successful approach. The location, release and evaluation of natural enemy impacts on population growth features strongly in his research. The evaluation of biological control agents are conducted primarily in the field and, when necessary, aspects of both pest and natural enemy biology and behavior are studied in the laboratory. &nbsp;He is also the director of the <a href="http://cisr.ucr.edu/" target="_blank">Center for Invasive Species Research</a>.</p> 
     <p style="margin-top: 1em; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 1.5em; line-height: 1.333em; font-weight: lighter; letter-spacing: 0.03em; color: #2668b2; padding: 0px;">Degrees<br /><span style="color: #444444; font-size: 12px; font-weight: normal; line-height: 18px;">Ph.D. Entomology (1996),&nbsp;University of Massachusetts</span></p> 
     <p style="margin-top: 1em; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 1.5em; line-height: 1.333em; font-weight: lighter; letter-spacing: 0.03em; color: #2668b2; padding: 0px;"><span style="color: #444444; font-size: 12px; font-weight: normal; line-height: 18px;">M.S. Zoology (1991),&nbsp;University of Auckland, New Zealand</span></p> 
     <p style="margin-top: 1em; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 1.5em; line-height: 1.333em; font-weight: lighter; letter-spacing: 0.03em; color: #2668b2; padding: 0px;"><span style="color: #444444; font-size: 12px; font-weight: normal; line-height: 18px;">B.S. Zoology (1988),&nbsp;University of Auckland, New Zealand</span></p> 
     <p style="margin-top: 1em; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 1.5em; line-height: 1.333em; font-weight: lighter; letter-spacing: 0.03em; color: #2668b2; padding: 0px;"><span style="color: #2668b2; font-size: 18px; font-weight: 300; line-height: 24px;">Awards</span></p>

     <p>&nbsp;</p> 
     <h3>Research Interests</h3> 
     <p>Biological control is the intentional use of host specific natural enemies (predators, parasitoids, and pathogens) by humans to suppress population growth of noxious plants and animals to levels which are no longer damaging. Many of our current agricultural pest problems are amenable to biological control, and when successful, natural enemies provide enduring, environmentally benign, pest control. Biological control is also being used in conservation efforts to restore natural areas invaded by exotic organisms, especially weeds. The emphasis of my work is to identify pest problems where biological control could be successful, locate and release natural enemies, and then evaluate natural enemy impact on pest population growth. Evaluations of biological control agents are conducted primarily in the field, and when necessary, aspects of both pest and natural enemy biology and behavior are studied in the laboratory. I am particularly interested in determining; 1) the magnitude of reduction in pest population growth caused by natural enemies, 2) the mechanisms by which pests and natural enemies co-exist at low densities, 3) the number of natural enemy species that are needed to give control, 4) inter-specific competition between natural enemies which utilize the same host, and 5) the economics of biological control when compared to pesticides.</p> 
     <br /> 
     <p><a href="/hoddle/harrysmithfund.html"><span style="color: #2668b2; font-size: 18px; line-height: 24px; font-weight: 300;"><img class="img_R" title="Harry Scott Smith" src="/images/harrysmith_thumb.jpg" alt="Harry Scott Smith" width="100" height="163" /></span></a><span style="color: #2668b2; font-size: 18px; line-height: 24px; font-weight: 300;">The Harry Scott Smith Scholarship for Graduate Biological Control Students</span></p> 
     <p style="margin-top: 0.5em; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 1em; line-height: 1.5em; padding: 0px;"><span style="color: #2668b2; font-size: 18px; line-height: 24px; font-weight: 300;">&nbsp;</span>For some time Dr. Hoddle has been facilitating the Harry Scott Smith Scholarship Fund to support graduate students in biological control in Riverside, CA. If biological control is to continue to prosper in southern California, the continuing recruitment and training of high quality students is paramount. If you would like to find out more about this scholarship fund or learn how you can support the Harry Scott Smith Scholarship Fund,&nbsp;<a style="text-decoration: none; color: #2668b2; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-bottom-style: dotted; border-bottom-color: #2668b2; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;" href="/hoddle/harrysmithfund.html" target="_blank">click here</a>.</p> 
     <p><span style="color: #2668b2; font-size: 18px; line-height: 24px;">Outreach</span></p> 
     <p>Mark Hoddle explains invasive species and the economic and environmental problems they cause in this lecture.&nbsp;Titled <a href="http://cisr.ucr.edu/mark_hoddle_lecture_invasive_species_california.html" target="_blank">“What’s in Your Garden? Protecting California From Invasive Species,”</a> the hour-long lecture, is followed by a question-and-answer session about popular invasive species invading California.&nbsp;</p>

Greenhouse Trials of E<em>retmocerus californicus</em>&nbsp;Howard (Hymenoptera: &nbsp;Aphelinidae) for Control of&nbsp;<em>Bemisia argentifolii</em>&nbsp;Bellows and Perring (Homoptera: Aleyrodidae) on Poinsettia in Northeastern U.S.A. &nbsp;IOBC Bulletin Vol. 19 (1) 79: 55-58.&nbsp;</p> 
     <p>4. <a style="text-decoration: none; color: #2668b2; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-bottom-style: dotted; border-bottom-color: #2668b2; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;" href="/hoddle/ccbcdisk_g000005.pdf" target="_blank"><strong>Hoddle, M. S.</strong>, R. G. Van Driesche, J. P. Sanderson, and M. Rose. 1996.</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;A Photographic Technique for Constructing Lifetables for&nbsp;<em style="font-style: italic; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;">Bemisia argentifolii</em>&nbsp;(Homoptera: Aleyrodidae) on Poinsettia. Florida Entomologist 79: 464-468.&nbsp;</p> 
     <p>3. <a href="/hoddle/ccbcdisk_g000001.pdf" target="_blank"><strong style="text-decoration: none; color: #2668b2; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-bottom-style: dotted; border-bottom-color: #2668b2; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"><span style="border-bottom-width: 1px; border-bottom-style: dotted;">Hoddle, M. S.</span></strong>1991.</a>&nbsp;The Determination of the Number of Larval Instars of<em style="font-style: italic; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;">Apion ulicis</em>&nbsp;(Forster) (Coleoptera: Apionidae). New Zealand Natural Sciences. &nbsp;18: 59-62.&nbsp;</p> 
     <p>2. <a style="text-decoration: none; color: #2668b2; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-bottom-style: dotted; border-bottom-color: #2668b2; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;" href="/hoddle/ccbcdisk_g000002.pdf" target="_blank"><strong>Hoddle, M. S.</strong> 1991.</a>&nbsp;Gorse Pod Susceptibility and Oviposition Preference to the Gorse Seed Weevil,&nbsp;<em style="font-style: italic; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;">Apion ulicis (</em>Forster) (Coleoptera: Apionidae). New Zealand Journal of Zoology 18: 31-35.&nbsp;</p> 
     <p>1. <a href="/hoddle/ccbcdisk_g000003.pdf" target="_blank"><strong>Hoddle, M. S.</strong> &nbsp;1991.</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;Lifetable Construction for the Gorse Seed Weevil,&nbsp;<em>Apion ulicis</em>&nbsp;(Forster) (Coleoptera: Apionidae) Before Gorse Pod Dehiscence, and Life History Strategies of the Weevil. New Zealand Journal of Zoology 18: 399-404.&nbsp;</p>

     <script type="text/javascript">

var calserver = "http://ragsm.ucr.edu/agsmevents/";
var prog      = "all";
var ishover   = false;
var autorate  = 7;
var animrate  = 'fast';

function scarousel_initCallback(carousel) {
  $('#jd_news_sidebar').hover(function() {
	ishover = true;
    carousel.startAuto(0);
    carousel.animation(0);
  }, function() {
    ishover = false;
    carousel.animation(animrate);
    carousel.startAuto(autorate);
  });

}

$(document).ready(function(){

  var path = document.location.pathname;
  var dir = path.substring(path.indexOf('/', 0)+1, path.lastIndexOf('/'));

  if (dir == "calendar") {
    $("#sidebar_events").hide();
  } else {
    $.getJSON(calserver + "ae_get_website_sidebar.php?jsoncallback=?&prog="+prog,
    function(data) {
      $("#jd_news_sidebar").html(data.sidebar);
      $('#jd_news_sidebar ul').attr('id','sidebar_carousel');
      //$('div.jd_news_scroll').jdNewsScroll();
      $('#sidebar_carousel').jcarousel({
        initCallback: scarousel_initCallback,
        vertical: true,
        scroll: 1,
        auto: autorate,
		wrap: 'last',
		animation: animrate
      });
    });
  }

});

</script>

      <!-- com.omniupdate.div label="maincontent" group="Everyone" button="707" -->

      <script type="text/javascript">

  var deptexp = "";
  var cname   = "sobadeptlist";

  function getCookie(cname) {
    var cval = $.cookie(cname);
    if (cval != null && cval != "") {
      return unescape($.cookie(cname));
    } else {
      return "";
    }
  }

  function setCookie(cname, value) {
    // note: this is a session only cookie, no expiration is set
    $.cookie(cname, escape(value));
  }

  function hideDept(dd) {
    $('#' + dd + '_body').slideUp(); 
    $('#' + dd + '_head').addClass("expand");
    $('#' + dd + '_body').parent().css('padding-bottom','0px');
  }

  function showDept(dd) {
    $('#' + dd + '_body').slideDown(); 
    $('#' + dd + '_head').removeClass("expand");
    $('#' + dd + '_body').parent().css('padding-bottom','10px');
  }

  function toggleDeptList(dd) {
    var ct = ":" + dd + "===";
    $('#' + dd + '_body').slideToggle(); 
    $('#' + dd + '_head').toggleClass("expand");
    if ($('#' + dd + '_head').is('.expand')) {
      $('#' + dd + '_body').parent().css('padding-bottom','0px');      
    } else {
      $('#' + dd + '_body').parent().css('padding-bottom','10px');
    } 
    if (deptexp != "" && deptexp.indexOf(ct) > -1) {
      deptexp = deptexp.replace(ct,""); 
    } else {
      deptexp = deptexp + ct;     
    }
    setCookie(cname,deptexp);
  }

  $(document).ready(function() {
    deptexp = getCookie(cname);
    if (deptexp != "") {
      var dl = deptexp.split(":");
      var i;
      var dd;
      for ( i in dl) {
        dd = dl[i].replace("===","");
        if (dd != "") showDept(dd);
      }
    }
  });

</script>

    <h2>Giving to the Eaton Collection</h2> 
    <!-- Start Sidebar --> 
    <div id="sidebar"> 
     <div class="nav"> 
      <h3 class="accessibility">Main Navigation</h3> 
      <ul> 
       <li><a href="/" title="Home">Home<br /><span>The Eaton Collection</span></a></li>
       <li><a href="/using.html" title="About the Collection and How to Use It">About the Collection and How to Use It</a></li>
       <li><a href="/about.html" title="History of the Eaton Collection">History of the Eaton Collection</a></li>
       <li class="currentpage"><h3><dfn>Current page is: </dfn>Contributing to the Eaton Collection</h3></li> 
      </ul> 
     </div> 
    </div> 
    <hr /> 
    <!-- End Sidebar --> 
    <!-- Start Content Area --> 
    <div id="main"> 
     <h3>Giving to the Eaton Collection</h3> 
     <p>To maintain its preeminence, the Eaton Collection welcomes monetary donations and donations of materials (gifts-in-kind) that add to the collection.</p> 
     <p>Funds donated to the Eaton Collection will go towards the preservation of its unique holdings, with an emphasis upon salvaging brittle materials. You can make a financial gift through our <a href="https://advancementservices.ucr.edu/GivingForm.aspx?DU=ORG16+-+University+Library">online giving portal</a> , or by contacting Head of Special Collections &amp; Archives, <a href="mailto:melissa.conway@ucr.edu?subject=Making%20a%20gift%20to%20Eaton%20Collection">Melissa Conway</a>.</p> 
     <div class="l_black_box l_address_block"> 
      <h4>Donating Books or Other Materials</h4> 
      <p>To&nbsp; donate books or other materials to the Eaton Collection, please contact:</p> 
      <address><span>Melissa Conway, Ph.D.</span><br /><span>Head, Special Collections &amp; Archives</span><br /><br />University of California, Riverside<br />P.O. Box 5900<br />Riverside, CA 92517<br />Tel: (951) 827-3233<br />Fax: (951) 827-4673<br /><a href="mailto:melissa.conway@ucr.edu?subject=Eaton%20Endowed%20Fund%20via%20website">melissa.conway@ucr.edu</a></address> 
     </div> 
    </div>

      <p class="footer_info"> <img src="/images/eaton/footer_eaton-collection_logo.png" alt="" width="79" height="90" /> The Eaton Collection is the largest publicly-accessible collection of science fiction, fantasy, horror and utopian fiction in the world. It consists of hardback and paperback books, pulp magazines, fanzines, film and visual material, comic books, and ephemera. It is housed in the Special Collections Department of the UCR Libraries, located on the fourth floor of the Tom&aacute;s Rivera Library. </p>
